BOTTOM HOLE LOCATION:

Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Sydney 14-9TFH
Figure 1. H&P rig #438 drilling the Marathon Oil Company,
Sydney 14-9TFH in Dunn County, North Dakota in September of 2014.
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company, Sydney 14-9TFH [SW SW Section 9, T146N, R93W; 401' FSL,
450' FWL] is to be drilled by Helmerich and Payne rig #438 and is located approximately 9.5
miles northeast of the town of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The
Sydney 14-9TFH will be a dual section well, with an approximately 10,000' long lateral
designed to further oil production in the area. The surface will be drilled using freshwater
drilling fluid, while the vertical and curve sections will use diesel invert drilling fluid. Well
plans called for the vertical section to be drilled to a kick off point of 10,268' measured depth
(MD). The curve would then be built at a rate of 12.00º/100' and would land in the middle of the
Three Forks Formation, target interval set by the Marathon Oil Company geologist. After casing
the vertical and curve, the lateral will be drilled using a salt-water drilling fluid. Geo-steering
and directional drilling techniques will be used to maintain maximum exposure to the target
zone. The planned lateral section was to be drilled south, at an azimuth of 1.13º. Upon
anticipated completion of the Sydney 14-9TFH, the hole will be prepared for casing and
production evaluation. The hole will be lined and will use a 30 stage artificial fracture technique
to maximize the production value.
OFFSET WELLS
Three offset wells were used as primary controls while drilling the Sydney 14-9TFH. Data
including gamma-ray signatures, from nearby offset wells were used to determine a prognosis of
formation tops. These wells include:
The Donally 11-16H [SW SW Section 9, T146N, R93W] is located approximately
50' from the Sydney 14-9TFH. This well was drilled by Marathon Oil Company in
August of 2014. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well and is currently awaiting
completion.
The Milton Guenther 14-9H [SW SW Section 9, T146N, R93W] is located
approximately 100' from the Sydney 14-9TFH. This well was drilled by Marathon
Oil Company in January and February of 2012. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well
and is currently active.
The Fleckenstein 21-16H [NE NW Section 16, T146N, R93W] is located
approximately 0.25 miles from the Sydney 14-9TFH. This well was drilled by
Marathon Oil Company in May of 2008. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well and is
currently active.
The vicinity of these wells to the subject wells surface location made them ideal for developing a
well-rounded prognosis of formation tops. The Milton Guenther 14-9H and the Paulson 14-9H
were also used for structure control during the lateral.
ENGINEERING
The Sydney 14-9TFH was spud on August 26, 2014 by H&P's rig #438. The surface hole was
drilled using a 13 ½" mill tooth bit and 5" drill pipe to a depth of 2,285' MD, in 4.0 drilling
hours. This assembly was also used to re-enter and clean the hole during rig maintenance after
the surface hole was finished. A freshwater based drilling fluid was used during this operation.
The surface hole was then isolated using 56 joints of 9 " J-55 casing set to 2,270' MD and
cemented to surface before beginning the remaining vertical hole.
The remaining vertical hole started on August 28, 2014. Freshwater was displaced by invert
diesel drilling fluid with mud weights fluctuating between 9.55-10.10 pounds per gallon. Using
two 8 ¾" PDC Smith bits the vertical hole was truly maintained at a 2.6º inclination to the south
using multiple magnetic slides to reach a kick-off point (KOP) of 10,300' MD, in combined 49.2
drilling hours.
The curve build began on September 01, 2014. A new bottom-hole assembly (BHA) was built
to begin the curve, including an 8 ¾" PDC Security bit, 2.12° fixed motor, and an MWD tool. A
trip was required at 10,536' MD due to issues with motor functionality and low build rates. A
new BHA was built including a new Security bit, a 2.42° fixed motor, and the MWD tool was re-
run. Another trip was required at 10,685' MD due to continued problems with low build rates.
A new BHA was built, including a Tri-cone Smith bit, a 2.50° fixed motor and the MWD tool
was re-run, and the curve was drilled to a total depth of 11,000' MD, in a combined 28.5 drilling
hours. 7" casing was then set to 10,983' MD using 127 joints of HCL-80 set to 5,827' MD and
116 joints of P-110 set from 5,827' to 10,983' MD. The casing was then cemented prior to
beginning the lateral section.
Diesel invert drilling fluid was displaced with a salt water based drilling fluid before beginning
the lateral on September 05, 2014. Mud weights were typically in the range of 9.80-9.90 pounds
per gallon. A 6" PDC Security bit was used along with a 1.40° fixed mud motor and an MWD
tool. This single lateral assembly drilled to total depth in 70.0 drilling hours.
The Sydney 14-9TFH reached a total depth of 20,843' MD on September 10, 2014, at a closure
direction of 1.00° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,793.86'. The bottom-hole location is:
9,932.25' north and 173.85' east of the surface location or approximately 204.21' FNL and
637.96' FWL, Lot 4, Section 4, T146N, R93W (Figure 2).
Figure 2. A map showing the spacing unit and offsetting wells for the Sydney 14-9TFH.
GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Geologic analysis for the Sydney 14-9TFH was provided by two Sunburst Consulting well-site
geologists. Gas levels were monitored using a digital gas detector and chromatograph. The
chromatograph was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder. The Pason relayed data
such as measured depth, bit depth, and pump stroke information to the MController gas
monitoring software. MController returned gas in the form of total gas units (100 units = 1%
methane equivalent in air) to be logged and displayed across the drilling location. Multiple
component gases (ethane, methane, propane, and butane) and their concentrations were recorded
in parts per million. ¼" Poly-Flo ® tubing was used to direct gas into the chromatograph where
the data was then translated and lagged to the correct depth. Rig crews caught lagged samples,
in 30' intervals, under the supervision of well-site geologists. Analysis and evaluation of gas and
drill cuttings began in the Kibbey Formation at 8,370' MD and ended in the Three Forks
Formation at 20,843'. Cuttings were observed in wet (isopropyl alcohol) and dry conditions
under a binocular microscope.
Lithology
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Sydney 14-9TFH; all depths while drilling the
vertical and curve are referenced to driller's depth.
At the request of Marathon Oil Company, logging began approximately 50-100' above the
prognosis top of the Kibbey "Lime", an interval of limestone within the Kibbey Formation.
The Kibbey Formation (Mississippian, Big Snowy Group) consists of red-orange siltstone with
some gray to red interbedded silty sandstone. There is a very distinct layer of limestone within
the Kibbey, referred to as the "Kibbey Lime", which was logged at 8,436' TVD (-5,955' MSL)
and consists of light to medium gray mudstone. There is a thin layer of anhydrite right above the
limestone that marks the top of the "Kibbey Lime" marker.
The Charles Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) consists of limestone and a large
amount of evaporates including salt and anhydrite. The Charles First Salt was logged at 8,590'
TVD (-6,109' MSL), marking the top of the formation. The prospective Ratcliffe interval is
located below the Charles First Salt marker and was logged at 8,998' TVD (-6,517' MSL).
The Mission Canyon Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) consists of gray to brown
limestone and was logged at 9,266' TVD (-6,785' MSL). Some areas contain algae laminations,
fossil fragments, and trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity and dead oil stain.
The Lodgepole Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) is characterized by light to medium
gray argillaceous limestone. The top was logged at 9,802' TVD (-7,321' MSL) and is marked by
a transition from limestone to argillaceous limestone. The "False Bakken" is a layer of shale
near the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation. It was logged at 10,649' TVD (-8,168' MSL). The
"Scallion" is a layer of limestone at the base of the Lodgepole Formation. It was logged at
10,659' TVD (-8,178' MSL). Several other Lodgepole markers were also used to determine if a
change to the landing target was necessary.
The Bakken Formation (Devonian-Mississippian) is comprised of two layers of black,
petroliferous shale and a mixed clastic and carbonate middle and lower member. The Upper
Bakken Shale Member was logged at 10,672' TVD (-8,191' MSL). This member is recognized
by its high gamma counts, petroliferous black shale, increase in rate of penetration (ROP) and
typically higher total gas units (Figure 3). The Middle Bakken Member consists of three distinct
lithologies and was logged at 10,689' TVD (-8,208' MSL). A layer of siltstone lies directly
below the upper member. Below the siltstone lies a laterally discontinuous layer of fossiliferous
(packstone) limestone. Below the limestone is a dominant lithololgy, consisting of gray to brown
silty sandstone (Figure 4). The Lower Bakken Shale Member was logged at 10,726' TVD
(-8,245' MSL). This member is very similar to the upper shale but it is distinguished by a
slightly darker sheen (Figure 5). The Pronghorn Member was logged at 10,742' TVD (-8,261'
MSL) and consists of a varying lithology sequence, including some siltstone, shale and dolomite.
Figure 3, 4, & 5. Wet cuttings of Upper Bakken Shale (left), Middle Bakken silty sandstone (middle) & Lower
Bakken Shale (right, 10x magnification).
The Three Forks Formation (Devonian) consists of off white to tan, microcrystalline dolomite
as well as lenses of pale green to pale blue-gray shale. It is characterized by a gamma signature
ranging from 50-140 (API) counts and was logged at 10,749' TVD (-8,268' MSL). The
dolomite contains trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity and spotty brown oil staining. The
shale is pale blue to gray-blue and contains trace amounts of oil stain in some areas (Figure 6).
Figure 6. Wet cuttings of sandy dolomite and pale blue shale in the
Three Forks target zone at 30x magnification.
Geo-steering
The well prognosis called for a landing target of 10,773' TVD at an inclination of 90°. The
landing target was set 36' below the base of the Lower Bakken Shale and 8' below the top of the
target area. Using gamma-ray data, well-site geologists were able to correlate formation tops
from the Sydney 14-9TFH to nearby offset wells in the area to assure an accurate landing. After
logging the Lodgepole top, the decision was made to drop the landing target 7' to 10,780' TVD.
The decision was based on the tops coming in consistently 4-5' low to the prognosis. A lower
landing was also desired to collect gamma data for future wells in the area. After logging the
False Bakken top the decision was made to raise the landing target to 10,778' TVD. Due to a
hard layer of pyritic sandstone high in the upper Three Forks, the location of the landing target
was meant to avoid any potentially hazardous drilling while remaining in a productive area of the
Three Forks. The actual curve landing came in at 10,777' TVD, landing the well-bore 10' into
the 12' target area.
The target zone top is marked by a cool gamma trough and off white, tan, and gray dolomite with
lenses of pale blue to pale blue gray shale in sample. Gamma-ray readings varied from 60-130
(API) counts while in target. The location of the target area put the top of the target 25.5' below
the base of the Lower Bakken Shale and the base of the target 9' above the top of the chocolate
shale.
The Three Forks target zone was entered at approximately 10,917' MD (10,767' TVD). The
well-bore was maintained in the target zone for 68% of the lateral. The formation dropped 12.8
of TVD over the course of the lateral, resulting in a gross apparent dip of -0.07° (Figure 7).

Gas and Oil Show
The label used to quantify gas for this well was units (100 units is equal to 1% methane
equivalent in air). The first time any significant gas was logged was a trip gas show of 40 units
in the Kibbey Formation. There were multiple gas shows from 28-63 units logged during
vertical drilling. Gas increased substantially in the "Scallion", and included a gas show while
drilling of of 3,223 units logged at the bottom of the "Scallion". There were multiple gas shows
around 100-3,200 units from the False Bakken to the curve landing, likely due to fracture
porosity.
Background gas in the lateral ranged from 100 to 1,500 units. Throughout parts of the lateral
there were higher concentrations of background gas and gas shows, specifically from 12,838'-
13,425' MD possibly due to a high location in zone and crossing of fracture porosity. Other
intervals conaining higher gas are attributed to increased zones of porosity. Trace amounts of
yellow-brown oil were observed over the shakers and was occasionally observed in the sample
wash. The highest gas show in the lateral was an off bottom gas show of 3,374 units and was
logged at 13,045' MD. The gas buster was not used during the Sydney 14-9TFH, no back
pressure was held, and no flare was observed (Figure 8).

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Sydney 14-9TFH is a Three Forks lateral well located northeast of
the town of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota. It was spud on August 26, 2014 and
was drilled to a kick off point of 10,300' MD. The curve was landed at 10,777' TVD, 10' into
the target zone. Preferred dolomite sections in the target interval contained fine intercrystalline
porosity and trace to rare amounts of light brown oil staining. Background gas in the lateral
ranged from 100-1,500 units, with gas shows as high as 3,374 units. Throughout parts of the
lateral there were trace amounts of yellow-brown oil over the shakers and trace amounts of oil in
the sample wash. The well-bore was maintained within the target interval for 68% of 9,998'
lateral section. The Sydney 14-9TFH well reached a total depth of 20,843' MD on September
10, 2014 after 15.5 drilling days.
Respectfully Submitted,
Nicholas R. Higgins
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
September 11, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A
detailed list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma-ray
marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined
wet and dry under a binocular microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from surface
casing to 11,000' MD, and changed to salt water from 11,000' to 20,843' (TD). Sample collection
began at 8,370' MD.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation [Big Snowy Group]
8370-8400 SILTSTONE: red-brown, occasional orange-brown, soft to friable, blocky, calcite cemented, poorly
cemented, sandy in part; rare SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to tan, fine grained, friable, sub-rounded, calcite
cemented, moderately to well cemented
8400-8430 SILTSTONE: red-brown, rare orange-brown, trace light brown, soft to friable, blocky, calcite cemented,
poorly cemented, sandy in part; occasional SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to tan, fine grained, friable, sub-
rounded, calcite cemented, moderately to well cemented

Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24406, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre
spacing unit consisting of Sections 4 & 9 T146N R93W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter
sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site
during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. MARATHON
OIL COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when contemplating
simultaneous operations on the above captioned location.
Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety
Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to
any producing well or oil tank." MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Ashleigh
Devenberg at 701-290-3277prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal
coordinate from the well head is: 9936 N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
William F Groffy
July 11, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck,
via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling
contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m.
to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

Gas Capture Plan
Sydney 14-9TFH
Sec 9 T146N R93W
Field: Bailey
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
The well is expected to commence production around December 2014. It is anticipated that it will be connected to
a gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
The well is expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the Sydney location. Flowback of the
well is expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 500 MSCFD.
Average Gas Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,200 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 700 bopd
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be between around 1,800 bopd
System Capacity and Utilization
Existing Gas Line
Capacity (MMSCFD)
Throughput (MMSCFD)

6 MMSCFD
well)
Gas Gatherer Expansion Plans
16" line will connect Killdeer and Lost Bridge Compressor stations allowing gas to flow to Oneok Garden Creek

Oneok Garden Creek II / III Gas Processing facilities ­ Q3 2014 / Q1 2015

Alternatives to flaring
Use of gas on lease, including fuel gas for Heater Treaters, is an alternative to flaring that is intended for this
location as well as connection to a gas pipeline.
Other alternatives to flaring are noted in NDIC order 24665.
